Programmatic Korea

 

Agency Cheil and demand-side platform MediaMath are partnering up in Korea, according to Campaign Asia, with plans for expansion into China and Southeast Asia next year. "We're seeing more and more programmatic buying growth from Southeast Asia, but so far, the markets showing the most potential are Japan, Korea and Australia," said Erich Wasserman, co-founder and GM of EMEA & APAC for MediaMath. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhPIcIwB21hCB3yslYbvifa0XHu4v9caTq9FxO3M3fk4oxQXe_YRXIvpzZ21kHSkqhJPKtG1ux4eyD1AHPJvPxAlNJpWwAMCSdpmTjdZGc-6VAZL1btQmT5NTi_JSYfz80Rf7iHfSb51zXr4-f3SecCR0ZONy62QW9LoCde2_x6kZ1m_8nfFibqlm0U4ZaZSl9gp14LC7irng-WYMIhVTkH53_2_S0VrZDgyLANOzJ-MzN7HpmvTfiAa1OzuZsUYxQXRW6M3Pj1otE5BjP7y_7A0> . In other Korea news, ZDnet reports that big South Korean publisher Daum <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhP-Zugacijik_TYL0mRXig2-OfP4-YNt5W_le5NMMWvYYQFEsWBgj5lLy7RPU3ej7C2CxleX444mgPQoaOhZTAqbkXGTHzRVi5w85Rr2iqTCw==>  saw increased display revs, but lower profits due to increased traffic acquisition costs. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhMF2fBDOJ5O9HdJTHtNsif9EWGvbwHFe8RvrprWdr3xy1mkbLr08ZJCBzU1bGhFDVx8rihfr0_hER4Z4XqiVphO7UTikiIOHcM0uuIiPFcnjWQzwFtcEv-m_T7FZHDmQwyTtff6pJsofRySVKeJZiLd6njN8AmDzQ07w9FTdEmdog==> 

 

Ecommerce Momentum

 

comScore says that Ecommerce sales in the U.S. via the Desktop grew 16% in the second quarter year-over-year. Among the highlights, mobile commerce is alive and well: "Apparel & Accessories was the highest grossing m-commerce product category with more than $700 million in Q2 sales, followed by Computer Hardware and Digital Content & Subscriptions." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhOmuG0j5P4sjjoKXnJhlG6brd7DGe1hNBeNuUkmzR86yrjxFh6dcCJSmO4qMeMsCnxl9uKuQhbYrMarLDYT1EyFjZK48rlURJRs7NISXfiKkxU1iYYv_PLqhQoG1xvOLCTTyBVstJ6WKSAyAqn9SjcUTBRyHMEiBy2riqqbgUzHsdu3d2fyN51bP0Zv_O6wWjTAuvDgtwf1I4XZ7At2qwY41W_ZeCmip_P0A4fgPPjVrifKbu93YMJsjky7iGmMtRk=> 

 

Mobile Drops

 

The mobile industry in Spain continues to struggle amid the recession, with carriers losing tens of thousands of customers each month, according to ZDNet. Landlines also continue to decrease as people try and cut back on spending, however, broadband subscription rates are rising. The major carriers are hoping that the addition of 4G to their networks will attract new customers and help with retention. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhNmPAQ_l_EHL6Zj-FQcQ2jY9uRT87keXh9BYQTwNphn7DtVDUouA-wSu6Pc-cEYO68KT5td_fTN3zMofgAFizuxGCrdCB-f0UW_0SWfGNjhNf_1Rhlh27rDW_t6GqqxEbuwo4-HXOJappkX0CTOZAtrabdDWV7UHHFavD0peWCPNXqDe4WCusD6> .

 

Recommendation Magic

 

Data collection has proven very useful for companies that rely on recommendations, such as Amazon and Pandora, but PandoDaily's Erin Griffith explores the need for transparency. She says that it helps if users understand why they're receiving a certain recommendation so it doesn't come off as creepy or plain wrong. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhNyXmKlueSXIB6x1Zj3Cf7MnxUsds-xk23zw-WbmT3EVZUXkPUe2hd9R2alxtSce93_dHUwwTyhDBodSxM0n2kOhX819A4Fxamn79hWkGzEVR0bOkCNun9X7dRCEh97h-VGXqxSJdogvftxm0bzV0zWv_IAYIlE9kESY8Tv73wC9h7M3sZ_bNtj7E1bji4KUYA75QrGxNGN6Q==> . Some companies are taking steps to make it clearer why users are receiving a certain recommendation, taking the risk of "ruining the magic."

 

Extending The Network

 

The programmatic world continues to barrel down into Latin America. Mobile ad network (soon-to-be exchange, too?) Millennial Media tells Baltimore Business Journal that they've partnered with a Latin American-targeted ad network, Adsmovil <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhO14k0pMzpPd5XQDtzxvhz1DH0GhXtULROTaBgKUjEAQ0IX-t5bJwyEl3Pxz9uRiqI2CBCJZS8t9D-wJGF6fZ68CDO3QpPn7II9jFL9omZcbA==> : "Millennial will allow Adsmovil to commercialize the company's mobile advertising products in Latin America. The area has more than 400 million mobile users and is a market Millennial has not previously been able to tap into." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhMRZiU6KW1eIIm12YCU8Z1t43pXbeWU2mCjmKhTqGoc0wnMApihGItyhtRpUp4gdiBBgipjwDpBhAjo-6dg__h0UA0nVSdvPDY7uMyMT3YsK3hTzLGFZK-sgzObBM5YissndFEmcFWdUkp97oz9UOT5iW0ljHfOVd5vz2eIrmli4kC1MsPWkbhjxlokZNP2TLbVyqI2wv5ZYQizmbASy07N>

Mobile Rich Media

 

Advertising agency DDB Chicago is expanding its mobile capabilities through a partnership with Celtra, a rich media mobile advertising company. Using Celtra's AdCreator 3 platform, DDB Chicago plans to "raise the bar" on mobile creative, explained DDB mobile exec Dirk Reints. "I think too often what a lot of brands and agencies do is try to squeeze online creative into mobile, and we want to have a mobile-first mentality," he said. "There are a lot of opportunities where we can integrate social with mobile as well as video and some other unique features." Read the press release here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhP5wCS8w8pUnUnZNtfkfcdBOEDtos4nvmxGJ7kbPmUPf9Db6rWqUkJHeTSJnWRq8WCZTxvhkz3yCrAUj7tPubpTRzPMohfV0rM15yNH2JId-9_kbAV6v4ZgxorP1KnK7KH-4pBeUdzOZDTqJUuWNjtNOxmm4GvXNqI-wsdswTH9XGs_E0tp68gwiiZqz7jBqwtbSw9clTeS0RPhutleQQ9jBlO9cWyOlSv2fNb9Ypw7SKgv5feEfxdU> .

 

Programmatic 101

 

Chango's Ben Plomion breaks down the current uses of programmatic in a column for Business 2 Community. The two most recognizable use cases are search retargeting and site retargeting. Although it left out some of the technical aspects of programmatic, the article tries to simplify it. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0011Zhkb4JpbhMI7PNhArExsGBhmFoqLY33qb9spNhmuPp5TlblocRGn6K-2rA7sjcXRnRZYjVCLPjAXerKh2pH0PP8ezY0RJFrX6C_efRKwQB4I9N87qaIcQJeKHv5W21cdygC0irHlN7OokOinAy4vKmL26LMFD3NF59pAo49Q6R-GILUbTHmt7YDy5CNIVy5FrdaZx5TYPQ9OvPwIL1spjghWgfutGVv5ipHh07ZqrBYgYycq5R4bQ==> .

Online Ratings Push

 

Nielsen is tightening its partnership with FreeWheel, ahead of the fall TV season, in an attempt to streamline its Online Campaign Ratings (OCR), according to Adweek. FreeWheel works with companies like ABC, AOL, ESPN and Viacom, and integration with Nielsen's OCR may encourage other traditional TV players to use the system. "[T]his will allow a seamless transfer of dollars to go from linear TV to the digital side and vice versa," said Doug Knopper, FreeWheel's CEO. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EmbvfPXFuP-YKs1wwnB_uTHfOGasKpxviLuAUe1lM9cGfKBn9kWcEJZ9feaWWeWVKjtPN_EmbF_P0Ubzz6eIYdRl_xA0ZNgbJlMUpwQ_mzJVUGSikipDPkW4-260otFhqt7Zr7atGy9Y9KpZ-OUbNXwHKX5xIv3KlXgmSwwC769uCjnLre8UVkBeHv0JgDAFM5XnLdJEzS_sRlOzXnWodUWNrFAXo-hZGBS1eDfMiV8=> .

 

CEO Search Over

 

Groupon started the process of looking for a new CEO, but decided instead to go with the interim CEO, Eric Lefkofsky, according to AllThingsD. "The business was functioning with much more speed and diligence and care and focus and we thought we had the right man for the job," said Groupon Chairman Ted Leonsis. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EmbvfPXFuP-dmQaxjRdAim9X6MtfEEE7VzD485IDliVB7ZZ-iHhi8OuQez8v81TkhVksAnVghx4WpWPzeEepy6Gi8wnAeRzT3JosaTtVVa5SBPKd-6liVLydgHPIxPElbipOO2AJACxcfysk_dprOuZY0laZuec91cVpPFg-rTgO9pjA2gHLpBKFdcZWIVbKVKwvTGKqJkigfIICYtv5BZY_VIHtk8U-> . Here's Groupon's earnings, which weren't bad <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EmbvfPXFuP9MiPAlsS7JQkPUBfGPlr4oFJCeESmbbAz2cVvjyD8VVQksXVmYxFwZiR0WfIhEgzqyjiWjAInvpkssVyFpximcfcw-pGrCz2GTxL7C_oJq4j3Lm3QcSsGIwAMmSdyeu2jruGeE3moJBoBV-Vdi5wzReH5yK3RwUiyMsMR-gWUOe7fomhl1oORJ_sv4a0uo_USq0LKB_h58m2I_bmv8CDOrt5CmRK-8HtM1lxEOAOVHJUY1i37W8tsRZ3gULfiU2I0=> .

 

NewFronts Success

 

According to an IAB survey, the Digital Content NewFronts were valuable to attendees. Seventy-eight percent of attendees said they walked away with at least one new opportunity for a company or client. What's more, 64% of ad buyers said "TV Plus Digital" buys would increase throughout the next year. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EmbvfPXFuP8Wa6EpqkFlMcRy9xYgjPbLf4ox3VEwO9GQ9Dfs6_TgNTr8Lb5QEUttdzcI261L5AWwW7LI-TvSqx6aSZtqQLkstRFEVsoYMHiuod43Xp_ZpJlFfr46X7QGKuj3nso2vdb2p8gcNCVHmOtiiTkR6ijjCAgfHilc-xBfkVshI701QrOxpbhg2nVzjkKfnapmBsShvcsF6PWUBjO61ww6hSS9FMaFa09tBJc=> . Local Follies

 

Tim Armstrong saw a lot of potential in Patch, but paidContent is reporting that a third of its 900 Patch sites are going to be shut down. PaidContent's Jeff Roberts reports that turning to automated advertising through AOL's existing technology may help keep the local news sites alive. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EmbvfPXFuP8xEHxHZAFREuviQPdznza-e-gYm0vZlN893-ozPETT4uicAUIrLonKf504kUi4vI4Bcf7j2_pX-iQ59gU9JcONylZQ9I-eWiVGrCYk0agLwrZgC4Wo14DiSVP68RYuS3nRJeBGvKXnHsmNm09nkecy0sBGtjuPOxvu12ehOCJRgY4Yf0gZ4AXc9jSTOCHTpq0=> . Jeff Bezos' intentions after buying the Washington Post aren't entirely clear yet, but former WaPo executive editor Len Downies doesn't believe it was done for vanity. He told Digiday it means "there will be a much stronger digital awareness, digital experimentation and digital vision in what's possible within a newspaper." Instagram's Indirect Payoff

 

Facebook hasn't rolled out any new ad products for Instagram directly, but the company still profits indirectly from it, as pointed out by James Borow on Ad Age. Facebook uses the power of its successful and popular newsfeed advertising to allow brands to use Instagram photos as ads. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EmbvfPXFuP8_fgEKzvXP9Klit0Lcldrjek2WRrjlYy9yexdfcND1BbvyUIVY9TygCr1GwfHbHmWTtgNEaA4VZgEt_AFy5eKvI4HZPrmDPwLFdCt5WIxyatrdn7SDYiuEXwxTpyowwWekVZyvnFim5k6NXFC95ZSePUzX1yuaNVEB0EAQJYMdPGgMPyca_5LY> .

Saving TheStreet

 

Elisabeth DeMarse brought Bankrate back from the brink of disaster, and now she's hoping to the do the same thing with Jim Cramer's TheStreet, according to The Observer. The company makes most of its money from subscriptions (about 85% according to the article) and the rest from ad sales. Immediately after starting DeMarse cleaned house and let go of 100 people, and replaced the entire ad sales department with a team from Forbes. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YnDzqwgK2SAaACAvXyLV_0x7Gg7tYlOeZe8oTVWrWCFDhnZA01lwFS9I8Q3y0B4eIFYtWuXiltpjDEK6TATapD9CJ6RavX7psEqyd2BLvkLAvvHejMGnx8fiS9EH1hIEpSDeuyrIhaiagMlXR9keE_3KaHWcUPL7nH-5siMREgc1MiF_8nRMpRRIvcT4KV_qw7Gy9yOZ9GVKAgPrtGftnuGQQdjqXWrL> .

 

CRM Is The New Black

 

MediaPost's Laurie Sullivan profiles V12 Group's new Launchpad platform. She writes, "It provides a complete view of all customer interactions across every type of marketing channel to more easily acquire new customers. Long term it will bridge the gap with CRM systems on one platform." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YnDzqwgK2SB7k9rcd2bg26fRGKJ8hlYrL6i9fSUiK-IRXvv_sJFIUODkxsibabrm0hC27U4KfVpcgBCPAJ9Fj1kMjfQW-VVwFGmCLMckfl5fh1lELRWOTHZS41ozwsZIfogIyzY0I1Orm3KzGPyAdrUKTJa2yhIR0M6MPvRw7zjLvmEKln47RhKc6DD63j2STr3MG8kacybBY3XV9WHdAbBhv_4EVO7iJZruHHDL7jzQ3U3_xhTxJh8sUN7W-RgY5RGMB9Bp4lw=> 

 

U.S. Merchants In Latin America

 

Internet Retailer released a report on 2013 Latin America 400, and found that web sales from U.S. merchants are growing despite challenges in the region. Companies like Wal-Mart experienced a sales increase of 150%, whereas Dell experienced a loss. Amazon has been testing the waters in Brazil by offering its Kindle and book services, but is still holding out on full scale e-commerce until it understands the industry better. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YnDzqwgK2SCSUVa-_OlJwziJoH9Yoh5idekt4cDU9BFIWbFiS36zTvkD0zIv5E1eIBg6cZ_tmwk8xVxS_0gEQO_e8cBoktFASCbLJXLtMzQQcWkRv9ZJdwQ01dTruQdA7jZfXgVhAQgxE3pnh9MK3cqopsTpkX1_oQ_k5b3vpIu00Flb45ULzVncqhDDgyRqlc-Tpxknvv3LT7DQ_jVRUw==> .

 

Battelle Speaks

 

In Digiday, Brian Morrissey interviews Federated Media's CEO John Battelle who says in regards to publisher Buzzfeed's growth, "It probably will end up scaling through much the same methods we're talking about now. You see BuzzFeed programs that scale through a network. That's still limited, and it's not programmatic. You don't have ability to identify an individual on a browser-based level. It's having that retargeted element that's important." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YnDzqwgK2SB_QxIMAaegChfWobp8u6zVmZ_qgqhk3zSUAndBCBuxqRBAsMGShEBKQUkE5JLpN6EYEVhMC85-NepVcF_zHvRLpU3c4q9l51kxF-OuhAmTSwP-DSrwPxkdKroZKnW-ftcrKEOBDkH0JTyZJm8Lwq4NTHMH5KvbkAEmoSb-AdcIKg==> 

 

Twitterbook

 

Facebook is starting to act more like Twitter by attracting celebrities to its site and encouraging conversations about public events, according to Peter Kafka at AllThingsD. Some similarities between the two are Facebook's introduction of verified accounts for celebrities, the introduction of hashtags and a trending topics section. Justin Osofsky, a Facebook executive, says the new initiatives will "unlock and surface the conversation about shared interests that's already happening." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YnDzqwgK2SA3rzHacDak-Ex64zQtsdANbPHZjd7UiXVMz2uAwhks6lt-I7GEw0UmCWQQbf_cbO0JGF-1hdfJjIVsCV2mUk2SZ-JY0k1lYtXfhrpu_NhnoBZJaPr7ZHwxW8ijJXjhaLyJNvfoVfjf2oK5CEgiuXv_R00Pm_yyfiKexZkbTAZoh7YqlcbsSnXwefUbQdTHpX5dQHkYXUa67ZzLVuPpUopKwj4aRNXRJS4=> .

E-tail vs. Retail

 

Mobile ad-tech firm Media Armor released its Q2 2013 report examining the differences between retail and e-tail shoppers. Ironically, one of the findings is that retail shoppers own more devices than e-tail shoppers -- and are also more likely to engage with a brand on a smartphone first. E-tail shoppers, however, are more likely to use all of their devices to make purchases. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCNUi96v_jv9OJ4_QiDOeBCidjQH5j4uv8lW0IayUQ4K18G_8NS8ZDsJEkl1Ndi0jqGWmZzYEAKEx68j5iVbmltFvorLCunFrn313M0miItTytt1GZe82iIL_1u4TCDMvZde0czFw1dqWsW6SNLWYyhA9Y9LinL6mAQGd6OaFEd_pw==> .

 

Whither The First-Party Data

 

Pulling from a recent research effort <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCOFwXlGQ59O6qj_ur3_9X0NU320BtyBCBhkbWQRFxiX0UYhSAEnXlhvH9_Ppo3JoKBgpoRehazdAs5St0NirKVxA9-hF2Hb0nY8p8SRSllYpWf2ZkxD_FSDboV8xNKw6ZA=>  by data-management platform and data exchange BlueKai, eMarketer makes some pretty graphics and pulls out a few observations along the way. An eMarketer blogger notes, "Fully 87% of marketers said they relied on first-party data (...) in making marketing decisions. The most frequently used type of first-party data was website data (83%), followed by customer relationship management (CRM)/registration data (79%), email data (72%), digital campaign data (67%), search data (45%) and mobile site or app data (28%)." See it now. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCMpYj9xQvCxzQUx_RPp3CpzqmE-4rBT2kuoXuW9WugE_gFQyP4RHqqvyur166BcR0aAkFXfhUvCTggIVH9M8liBlEaErWGqZ6IV5o2POJWTxsEZYZwI2zQMaP6pv-iSXyRV9BliX4y4_WqlL0a7K01YjQW546b7ILnxZsdFd8yalZRBc13TUK3MnnzucX7GTes=> 

 

VCs Just Don't Understand

 

Getting funding is crucial for a lot of ad-tech startups, but according to Digiday, there is a gap between what VCs want to invest in, and what is actually possible. For instance, a lot of VCs don't understand the need for a service layer, which is still crucial in the dynamic advertising world. "They don't get why the model can't be an enterprise technology one with completely self-service tools," said Fahad Khan, CEO of social tech firm One Public. "The reality is we're dealing with 24-year-old media buyers and we still have to do some of the lifting. That's what VCs don't want." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCOr4P7NnJ1E-JtSrWcY5THXdqlMq1kdAEM9h2YeyUHXs-4R2Bg2WAr9yT-0hAJPA_d-48jSKbpuSePqLp4FtpXyiVlQpVT_aLJ9MpFa_b7WBvZ0DqBpx1pQiY9FUzFgR35Wrwn3FHNtK9hMeeP0992RgU47uJIHXXI=> .

 

New CFO

 

Yesterday, the former online ad business of Rapleaf continued to transform through its progeny, LiveRamp. The company announced that it has hired a new chief financial officer, Bryan Morris, who comes from video ad firm Ooyala, where he was VP of finance. According to their boilerplate, LiveRamp helps companies onboard their CRM data online for addressable display advertising purposes. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCO62iORI7hAG1l_BCl6Q59noqHZXEnaKnfewkBs-09VRJ-RcrhINWNFOIuvLIDCJNplxKdIqCOTw_Jtnh4EboC_Qry_oVzUkrcAg488F7BvYrRK6UqU7xev5kpqfRE5pX4Yg-9aJplqnx3QgSJh16nZfGCZ2MFxLauuli6Pi2iGsZ1rDiJqqGiS5nw7rkRpsmDymYLyYI1eDxt3jHzWKVyD> . Also of note... an ad-tech trend: hiring a CFO. The reasons could be several: prepare for an IPO; prepare for an acquirer; C-level oversight on finances looks good for the brand; or something else?

 

Driver Data

 

Dash Labs hopes to take geotargeting on the road by tracking users while they are driving and tying that data into mobile offers, billboards and more. The technology would be similar to what Progressive uses for its Snapshot feature, tracking driving habits and giving users a discount for being a good driver. Dash aims to make the product more than just an advertising opportunity by indicating to users when they brake too hard or providing more information when the "check engine" light comes on. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCP9-_b9QQgAZnnFTwsv4mexwlhmFTjwI2bq_OPkzGe_rFjPEgBBxVddkz6Dy6ANM9koY6R3_9xwnT3qAtTYFFg1T-Ponsk5HgeHwAqylPW-06hCfMVlmpIyhgURzWMtEe0EQMXKmxnA_PKKxytet-YF2T0DlwUB0P72h3nvaoghCOdPibCKgH4O8TkHnikyONskjKW1fy4CHptYW03vRZ6W> .

Define "Premium"

 

On iMedia Connection, Netseer CEO John Mracek takes a crack at defining "premium." He concludes, "The rules of premium no longer apply as, more and more, the ad world adopts programmatic media buying. I'd say it's time for some new math, where premium, exchange-based inventory equals relevance plus the assurance of brand safety." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCMUYu_z7tZpyJY-XEaFA49tv8k9IsqPPEzs3b4cqKJfun5n4hWO_DJQhdAPdeE6uR4id0qxYizeA9mhU3ynfkzrTYNHhjR5EXDkMgDjX3TU83edfX3Pxi_JvwC8PpNm1yvfgRXn5A7gwevT7yog6MZ2> 

 

NYC (Ad) Tech Boom

 

The candidates in the NYC mayoral race should pay close attention to the technology industry, according to PandoDaily. Between these tech companies thousands of jobs are being created, and the industry is booming. Companies like Google, AppNexus and Facebook were called out for adding the most jobs, among many others. "The consumer tech startups get all the glory, but in New York, the ad-tech startups are getting all the talent." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017GqsvyJMMCOWPqq2Db6wc03yJyaDtnIwfyPVS8XIV95x3hexjxvWTEsDfnF4MRt6QY4l8alf4Enlb6itnhYa5W2vExZAwRxRWZ3twiJgfWw5eCHXexHDnApMnWZdz1Tcc0EpYoGwF4zBS8QflRBGwDDR5xdeWXhSSaA3FBp0ypvjP_POKXe7GQ1DtghVGWaR4Z79sqmczjgMUlKa-7IBFA==> .

Blinkx Acquiring Video

 

Blinkx snatched up Grab Media before Yahoo got a chance, according to TechCrunch, for an undisclosed though likely small amount. Both companies operate in the online video space, connecting video producers with an audience. "This transaction, while modest in size, enables us to meet growing consumer demand for online video, and provides us with an established platform to distribute and monetize these interactions across desktops, tablets, smartphones and connected TVs," Blinkx CEO S. Brian Mukherjee said in a statement. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYTby2RaKU9xkCzSXOwmnaEUVy4O8XnhvDYmuRF83ZycIgi9TO63sqLbO0Y0Obe4deRUrmAex9DuapKdM-PY78eT38XB-VffEsMVcRgz7cJN4w5eOEm8O4Q7h2-4AhTAaLwbxr2k5btogLZM_C-FWcha9PvE34wOO1xp0U0PCBBPyw==> . Way back in 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYQ2VZSDoguJyr7WrR5PxckhVBq5rC6k_9OQBGrKvMcNss7ZUtyhDP3ruGnSXBQ358Lwhu4ddFhkRNo0wUlLld2aN9oEu6ftPQmTDTjCHF6TBdG59LqeSFnoO8yJIiQF2anok_vslqd0PcY7rdCrkEPDDcs1XBV4MxJSxo7W5HzN-w==> , Blinkx bought ad network Burst Media.

 

Brand Cohabitation

 

The Publicis Omnicom merger gets still more analysis -- this time from the conflict angle. In the article, six major accounts are dissected, including the infamous rivalry: Pepsi vs. Coca-Cola. None of the competing brands were willing to comment, but Michael Kassan, chairman and CEO of MediaLink, points out that some of the competing companies have cohabitated before. Read more in Ad Age <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYT7v0QB07wJhGs7Y3O0JBvIjd7bCaxTE1Uybjs2X7k9eRJpcooaYjzbl-Xv1BytLnTlkAM2B2wEOSw2wGhn3LL1i8sUZPyogd6C04JATHaolW3bgqQlQL2PNGNX5N0WpojUzEaLM8kcpnFL6fzobKYi8FnZFIy5Vht0duY0rWvPWvbL_NO1OKS3LWdyfsFfA3ZocFD49KPI_w==> .

 

YuMe Prices IPO Wednesday

 

A month after YuMe filed its S-1 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYTJUj9vC7jurYyNn7s5F9btvLP26-94kFPDnnzT5Nudh-rbg3mu-J7YRovPqL-NkiHRkE72vlxy4ODdCsvjW_MCNCXddTuq4eMeR2K8FSC7AmOGZs1sZQijArL-pXJTyHFPpapyG5vCCNP-blkyfqy0-FlBpstlocBXKX8x2qnTJDkNr1DtBKHPYPDZO9bOr9o_bdk_ls6_0A==>  with the SEC to join fellow video ad tech player Tremor in the public markets will get its chance to see if investors are still hungry for more of the same. While Tremor's stock has recovered in recent weeks after failing to raise the $90 million it initially hoped for when it went public a few weeks ago, YuMe's profitable position <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYTMIcTAL_TTR7UJgIREHoGSh9EIspFT_GzU-z3F8FCUUW1RcY5W7sKpPcwV2u8ZMPnlWx4dmi8o4tulzEnstf0sSYpTaWzCbwjVAZojKLrY_BAYWBUDqEKB-MJEGn4M8HbD6QV3kw0Is3jEegLATJq5hH143qO_tHYwfC3QfcSjgqDYjAc-CbwlFCIOQrZ0d8mXkgX2iLKRoQ==>  and double digit revenues suggest that it should come close to getting the $65 million it's aiming for with this sale.

 

Digg The New Native

 

Although native advertising doesn't have a single definition, most publishers have been approaching the format in a similar fashion. Enter Digg, acquired by Betaworks last year. The company is taking native advertising and giving it a twist: the ad content is produced by the editorial staff, Digiday is reporting. "Rather than speed dating, brands can work with a point person at Betaworks to develop custom campaigns using the best parts of products," said Mike Rothman, head of monetization for Betaworks. "It looks like a media company where you have some kind of in-house service capabilities in addition to amplification platform." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYT5S_GazQl8U0-HEPUFwYPwD_jNZd52LKDLKExhMkktZptKtvo8ZpCqxsoJWWfzZe6dqu0WSJAUBcdKT_I5qqZEAwWiVW7pVDfLoaHJB3V8fptvSuQjNxY20mBxyl4mWMAdFcn55w9F1A==> .

 

Twitter Advertising Review

 

The Twitter advertising platform has evolved over time, giving advertisers more robust options for targeting and reporting, says Clix Marketing's John Lee in a think piece. He matches the different methods for advertising on Twitter along with what he sees as some of the best practices -- including the lead-generation card feature to its self-serve platform. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYQBas9ym5rast0SvfOdymrnIgY39baHBE6uUQBUdRJ7xrX11dWwwKbesFlHyhTPel8zND-6OjAaf4JQ2sZBAG9HFOHmOgi38aSqpUAE3_J9ZWHdX_MvS3SXvGSkeD2KFFIdotJeQwS0KDi8NlEogZ-VuFrhQBtVYdP2FS9e6QH0dEO5mwhjOgmvuMDBLLwVdUo=> .

Programmatic Without Cookies

 

Programmatic advertising is in its infancy, but with the growing tide of privacy concerns leading to a potential end of the third-party cookie, automated advertising will have to adjust. As Stuart Colman, managing director for EMEA at Maxifier points out in a column for The Guardian, this gives publishers with rich first-party data an advantage, and alternative methods to tracking users besides cookies are being tested. He writes, "When it comes to tracking and privacy, we need to move from a 'one-size-fits-all' approach to one that is flexible, multidimensional and - above all - consumer-friendly, allowing consumers to change their preferences and feel more in control of their browsing session." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYSCf7f-mzowk8uEMZ-ZP4I3FzasPv0FpUUR1bLg6Ucmd_ZrEB-uyDL1UklRAny1je_pU7rslVDETQYzbs49wbMkUDVuPxWbBefSEn_vVMtbpA7Z8PGRtQNDhTEuHNTNj7CDLkVMo9rIaHzjZ1hT6aAFtDREoV1I_k3imUaTSQ3EvKH1Eovu52j2k_4fO2ls-x7Twsr6hfLzmVE3J_DfxBbo0fie-7GjwMnohP2TuOJ0cw==> .

 

Global Match Up

 

Accenture wants e-commerce. The consulting firm and hybris have teamed up to address multichannel e-commerce on a global scale, according to a press release. "As hybris' global strategic partner, Accenture can help bring the hybris' omnichannel commerce platform to companies that have struggled to implement worldwide transaction solutions that can be tailored to local country needs," said Anatoly Roytman, EALA managing director of digital consulting for Accenture Interactive. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001riLi5Lr4mYQThT13ckjSEBRGuuZb37zuDSyu8Zq4uBmeOnvI0pZ95GTyVep6QVVqKwKnPs0fsdWrYpvPQ-2yCe5gIv7Y1KsnRabqOtx3MxEhwaDcWrR8hIv-sm0YUQ6zEnFt63hcpvh3dpk6jZjFEkgr8E8tpA-eauhqG0yAHUUI6v5c0PWu3qixHZpeccNH44ImHHrNa4EZbqMESsPWFgOM7_n8AwVZiptyZojL7-flmFWYXpDv_jBCRNC1kB6-SG6s0voXzsI=> .

Farming Out The Click

 

The Guardian details the dark world of "click farms" in Bangladesh that look to generate clicks -- often with social media objectives. The Guardian's Charles Arthur says, "For the [click farm] workers, though, it is miserable work, sitting at screens in dingy rooms facing a blank wall, with windows covered by bars, and sometimes working through the night. For that, they could have to generate 1,000 likes or follow 1,000 people on Twitter to earn a single US dollar." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7IPQwLF62cx0sGCbCpxQ_0KdvFxw5Ci5NYOu8TgDmZbDWYcGCOXHa1fggy7DmhZXb5XyvPaPWKemKmlF6T7PBH0JI_--Ok9t7WvNbE7Dgdr3QUX4x57_rBM3BN-ipIp7ZpbIAB5FBgg1l9QqLaFwahSaVJ0QeSvei1cawbUvoi6HWuDM-wnu1HDA7o66_-JUIpBiTJwAxfcvyzuMnmFN3H_> 


Programmatic Merger


Traditional ad agency executives are sweating bullets according to a new article from The Wall Street Journal. Mike Sheehan, chairman of integrated agency Hill Holliday says that he can understand how "creatives" feel left out of the conversation about the importance of data to the Omnicom and Publicis merger <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7IqU2CXj-tTtHiVelrSaXYN3mD0WJqBiiKYrytXZXPENpTvafb9_IdO-yEB2jGl7ol7brbx1QcIgY6ejR65JnP-CqpkYwEyMEHeSRFdAnkPnYwTCSBqzLrSo1syi_LwrafgDWpaAtUxHmYNratPIP_SwDV3u9TJ4x4Km0idxL9v1RBY2UtbMwRT8a1SWNNRcMS94N4y-eWBEhcE_3EIf8q_EXm-sJuDIe1amq7rpww8Ww==> . He tells The WSJ, "Algorithms cannot give people goose bumps, and algorithms cannot tell a story, (...) cannot give you that nugget of insight that differentiates brands and products. That is only performed by human beings that can tell stories and can understand consumer behavior instinctively." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7IuMv47shd8YjDzcEiaXSKceRyDgdNpaUtFjlQ3mLukC4uavxk1IsIhd5e6ttVQafuT-VmF69duVYq5sHbSGzjGC5QLXVk9QZomygVuiuacHDqEwKNi2ThonEpLPlkAowA1Qtv1iJ6v0OdlSmI4qiBhzn0I3dKh4FbvW5OlhL7QbinIdlyyEVBr> .

 

Blue Icons

 

Although Twitter received praise for its privacy-friendly approach to advertising, Ad Age notes that the company doesn't use the AdChoices icon. "AdChoices started as a solution for banner ads when native advertising was still just a glimmer in our eye," Jordan Bitterman, Mindshare's chief strategy officer, said in an email. "One might argue that an AdChoices logo tagged in a tweet is not the right solution for that platform. The logo would be everywhere, which would be a poor user experience to say the least." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7K9qN5tQY0bnKCXLsdE_QZ52Gq14lKKkADmfzRXKtDt6yn7pVlI9BP9ZjEZED9ErOlRQ9ozQjt5SipwpxRRe0ty0eGFYLJQe1olxwow1zH7HmW7pIHRq1NMyGnUu4-3m2IiXhsBzPUgmREkBNZqhXhccugIjU5wei_DiijVxbB8aUzj0Qb4LpdiuKLZQ3RjE5FALrx3lst8rw==> .

 

Economies Of Scale

 

The Economist explores the major points of the Publicis Omnicom merger, calling it the end of the "Mad Men" era and the start of the "Math Men" era. Television advertising may still be king, but display is rapidly catching up, with Google and Facebook leading the charge. Large agencies like Publicis and Omnicom are trying to stay alive by getting even bigger, hoping sheer size will be all they need to stay ahead. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7Lq8gMjaMRAn4wRp6gLEumKZXWxK4Nuir3WejOJ0pPMwyzPfgcXeHESUNJS3qFommi0DQJLQggnc4Rm54C-B3laMV5jwHrtDGdEi4mNmdGS2gBuLKr65Zlx0S6kQUfmkIYltzcS1tC9yM9VIw_TaU_MVkWJhUtInR6p6DQS_ZcfwT6JXsZEbaz9-_RIc8WsjzF86J1GishOiyrbxajQBSm4lFylCE7j6O7WNNgNBv5bzWm1FGNydDVA> .

 

More Mobile For Yahoo

 

The Yahoo acquisition spree continues, this time with the purchase of a mobile-browser startup called Rockmelt. According to Kara Swisher on AllThingsD, Yahoo paid $60 million-$70 million for the company, which will help Yahoo in its quest for mobile greatness. "The team has built a simple and beautiful technology that combines social, personalization and discovery to help you not only find what you're looking for, but also stumble across some cool stuff along the way," Mike Kerns and Adam Cahan wrote in a company blog post. Read both stories here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7Lbg0rnPTLI0-Exec87pNJDTGk9Puk5Y_A0nKCz-D-4I-eO9mMux_D2-SyjIQcNMWwKsYG_ikhx5dAxyoGzT_HiX3PUl6r9NDfCIcONA19HSSf5XTUgmj_8bjxsb-pAURIyMaJGaObPiYU2LNEko34y95aiR7MlKydQBl5KBmu-f-cBEv1s16WUr9Xcr1kWQmE=> , and the blog post is here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UYGMZt0IP7LLitBceYxNcagyRN7N4ADEXlbHd6s2g1BAwL760Ltz6yc4x2xLvPbBvx95solGkt3onbaL_JgqtkxS2nnrXNCkiNw8taTdEj6r-XKK3uRkg02_oVbKNCEQmjcTQkfa3vCO0VUJsZxs8PFlny71r-UwlEDd3FfbL3jqv08SLHzxMRFSYzGJuoff> .

Social Shopping

 

Social media has presented a huge advertising opportunity for retail, but it still pales in comparison to search and email, according to Mashable. Facebook and Twitter, despite boasting large audiences, don't give luxury retail brands the kind of lift that traditional CRM does. However, social sites Instagram and Vine seem to be garnering much more engagement, so it's not time to give up on social altogether. The Long Road Ahead

 

Businessweek attempts to answer the question on everyone's mind: Can Marissa Mayer save Yahoo? After one year at the struggling tech giant, Mayer has made plenty of headlines through big acquisitions and sweeping policy changes such as ending telecommuting. But her main focus has been on mobile. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwbLfrMgO-HY1JQIJIn3ukGo5Boxw9DOdShRDq9SCUvQ5tTbPiSnaeW2qrnFaPz35_Wt-hSniukyAHPMrdl2v5oRB2RnRTdmhDhsSgNM2VYjLOtJuIXFbo0Avmd0Q80t7SxvjRZGjCAXTeYj9T0EPuDQschqgsEB1woNa2lk-mGZI0zskrahu1Wi> .

 

Funding Run

 

Run raised $1.5 million dollars in funding from Verizon Ventures, TechCrunch is reporting. Although the DSP takes a mobile-first approach, the company also offers cross-device ad buying. It's the 3-year-old firm's first outside investment. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwZVCBufkW1AeEm8hEK0VBC20ALt0yYDsSEHnd_scy3pXfqJ1Rqdeuh3R76dy7R68wI03dXrKQlYWjSe8-e2lQS2Bhat2Y2-e7D434YUkybj7hOV5fIdx5kDtgmTxEwrJOhp_uFLXKVafSPa_nkV_GFAe2NPOUjIEI8=> .

 

Targeting Misconceptions

 

Despite its best efforts, the Direct Marketing Association hasn't fully educated people about the difference between behaviorally targeted ads and regular ads. According to MediaPost, the DMA has gotten several hundred complaints from people about behavioral ads. Only problem? The ads actually weren't targeted, and therefore no tracking opt-out was possible. However some complaints did correctly identify targeted ads where users couldn't opt out, exposing potential problems with the mechanism. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwZbv8lDYcdQVJ1LQUoBZr08g_cT_dfDeMyxeqpbpTRDneb7xNblb9RVd-cldRhH65n_w-BVgVve4r7AGxxI8fefcPECPXh5ggmVwD8r1Tnhm9PuoO9kn30rOVDykkNuXkt_NTU9y8XDc_xcT9gaFewof5DMNANMuehzEVVb06y68OC1Y3ixw1YM1Ci_wDpOqwqvJvwWDmkFa_7Gcj6Brs2lO2Ycw-xHDjXAEJS6O8AiiMD5erzeikDdx58x6GL_Wjo=> .

 

HootSuite Money

 

HootSuite raised $165 million in Series B funding for international expansion, especially in Latin America and Europe. The company could be a dark horse in the social ads space, having been named one of Twitter's early marketing partners. According to GigaOM, the company also may make a few acquisitions -- no specifics though. "Our focus during the last couple years [was] on just building this business on social media," CEO Ryan Holmes said. "We've effectively gotten to where we have in just under $5 million in the company." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwZO-bXAszBlEuYaHG6tASjhuuBIEiNk4TMmbk0jSThpZ3U1J0QbEB0MxxjQFnuFOh-dLdLs-BWk7UDEkmRgkSxslnwvdggZOUKC46cNvpkskqHt87sc2JlmWYw3WiI7gOAO6oaiJEZfimPiD8HieI_6fk0cVXYYySDSx0Q0cYMUF84yWrvP0F8AA9EipI8ZC0jXTKv-zAC9cMRCrP-reeegvMQKRDQxrbw=> .

 

Forever Ago

 

Two years is a long time in the tech world, and Doug Weaver gazes into the past to re-evaluate his "Dougorithm" for The Drift. Some major changes that he noted: Ad networks still exist, trading desks didn't meet their full potential and the private-exchange concept evolved. Then he asks a very relevant question: What will the ecosystem look like in 2015? Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwY_ON-O-8S1r2qW-cvsn2LRc_ChfFj9M4UjCBXcbnrKQ2xtZCsYffgII90l-Egl_nX_F0p6OUMfWXv1K71Trk2bx58s5khMqKisACrkS11CYV_qRVJMcXDaGoxh4rwnoA8NM0S4Tz4AEWwrEk8McS2V> .

Amazon vs. Pinterest

 

Amazon is going to head to head with Pinterest with a new "Collections" interface. As Pinterest further secures its place in the e-commerce space it seems Amazon is ready to use imitation to stay competitive. TechCrunch reports the feature has been slowly and quietly rolling out since April and is now available to the public through the account tab. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwZaZHFvnES1eqPGi4yzXP7XSnVaOp_kMdzHO_5sHY84CKwdLnC8YeG5zcGYt-gsof2emoUlbYcyOYVu8XCP-zFzMXNqgXEkNu1HKlGVYkuK3UahFLKCnCAWbHVE6Vct-a8EpG5WvaV5AMSCq9NalggnJzAZRU2ml1dVoPbdpcZkhkROZSt__lfZuBKsZIv21jwLYdOFmtz-rVR6aYzRZ8wEXKwyVHrshwqD8VxA6ryLBA==> .

 

Crowdfunding Video

 

Two crowdfunding startups, Patreon and Subbable, allow users to pay for video content they love rather than exchanging their attention for it. As the founders put it to AllThingsD, ads view everyone the same way: as merely an impression. But if users truly love the content, they will pay for it. "I don't think ads really properly value content, because they don't take into account whether a user cares about that content," said Jack Conte, co-founder of Patreon. "It's a binary rubric; they're either watching or not." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_Op2hUNIhwYJz5pQg1UbGLIOJFhEJ6Cs_K4P6LjG3qnzddUnfgZWj76nzSiQM-a94ceKlNw8Cb_4yg9xp1UVZeEFVRotjHR8xxPos6HJoO8yd1mgBM1zX85RlX4ezpR7pEMxbmVbJUJcCEGu62Ox-p12bkWKZ53OGx0XeS181l5Od4kpFnxIgsm8nLPeh01O_X5w6UxNtPfkpcaOE6fHE0tXsgoo_wzMNVDU-MhIc1s=> .

Publishing Agency

 

Agency holding company IPG is launching a new publishing division, called Mediabrands Publishing, according to The New York Times. In an effort to reach millennials who aren't as easily marketed to, the new division will allow brands to push out unique content. "Producing content that's relevant to your audience is actually really hard, especially if that's not a core competency of what you do," says Sony exec Susan Jurevics in the releases. Ride the  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X3R9b1L-y2bKiLJ9yqTqRbSq4dc78NLhWxie503TMm74oMIowTO_HWhJPFKvjHMuHqJX8vgjt3ZZ-3iyT1KDxCOpxUfylyT8c3qLQeHHnJ47ue9QnWO9xSJ6hVoSwhPqhkEUfIzfjv0j2kxhZka6dIOIvpx9lzTawxLURGnrn0JRNKIyU2OTd59pluWVnHADRzcXFATQ0h_pSiQ_kfbqvpu8fsziCxDv9blwjtEDYNY=> "native" wave.

 

Data-Driven Partners

 

Foursquare and Turn are teaming up to harness the power of check-in data, Ad Age is reporting. Neither company commented on the partnership, but Foursquare CRO Steven Rosenblatt has said advertisers won't be allowed to target consumers on a one-to-one basis in the past. Foursquare generates buckets of valuable location data, of course. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X3R9b1L-y2b3RG1cEmEh1p59GyX7i6dExOxbejMYBdLd5Xp_LVGSA8nqkuU2ByoxTx3iK3ybB80yXYS5ujg8dcVOhs3rtm2e5ssb7AU89re-sxMZ6nsQwC7lZ9sLmv2rEr9Il0rnm_ZXrRgfjHFi82gD6PWViyviDXHZ7mPOhYhX1ZIZ44UMPwTOw_YCv_PY7blAQEWLCRpKNPRk4LAS_g==> . Everyone wants a way around the cookie.

 

Nielsen's Take On Facebook

 

Nielsen pushed out a press release touting its measurement tools after Facebook announced its television-style advertising product. According to a Nielsen study commissioned by Facebook, advertisers have the potential to reach an audience comparable to or exceeding the four TV networks it measured. The other important takeaway is that brands have the potential for duplicated reach (reaching the same consumers online and on TV). Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X3R9b1L-y2ZIoRkuFdCZEQuk6DjBQykuqG_SeumSclmbD2yqyUFRCVg0H3K7sRsc9VYo-VCEYCTNyUYzGII2LwiSGD7L5Y6J0z6-60P06bZol0hGc13eK37kGKQ5pMu9-FOLmkZqgcsJ-fT5OiVIm7jA0piK2OgPWZKBdhqyw1fYrn14WhHn4KXKNGMB0nAmLB9q-KO6m_iyawSND0ObAqWjG2gozypVWp_0FV3JKyWc7cYrrjRuMg==> .

 

Loyalty Index

 

Although app downloads decreased slightly, according to its data, Fiksu said in a release that the cost to acquire a new user went up by 17 cents to $1.50 and much of the increase can be attributed to the competition among Facebook's advertisers. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X3R9b1L-y2ZgxLURGa7MwrDVFkh6pzwESQ-nQfBcMPCqUbutAeDrh5Z4FKzBQ-5hb0BN8KDQTSFD0vKQnR8CW9JCoU-YtRgGCIRuBIpIHwFW_-zjmzeNN37AJXDl17gIQKPqeEee54W6hFQ2N-MzlnDPcCpnDkquNDQmP1a6WATowVYnLsD4jPDz5V8N1chMX2skvLQa6hWzPtyWcyD2Q2fj_hexgX28Dj_U9tlUr4Y=> .

 

Privacy Line

 

Amidst increasing pressure for companies to be privacy-friendly, Google has been walking a tightrope with its big pair of ad-tech ballet slippers. And, according to The Wall Street Journal, a setting was in development across Google services that would allow users to decide how much information they wanted to share using a slider. The three settings were minimal, medium or maximum, but apparently the tool has been scrapped for a number of reasons.
